  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a9fb092d-e8b1-4d47-9eae-2553c21edb69'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12784538430254661204">The Amber Room is one of the greatest treasures ever made by man: an entire room forged of exquisite amber, from its four massive walls to its finely crafted furniture. But it is also the subject of one of history's most intriguing mysteries. Originally commissioned in 1701 by Frederick I of Prussia, the Room was later perfected Tsarskoe Selo, the Russian imperial city. In</span>
  <span id="freeText12784538430254661204" style="display:none">The Amber Room is one of the greatest treasures ever made by man: an entire room forged of exquisite amber, from its four massive walls to its finely crafted furniture. But it is also the subject of one of history's most intriguing mysteries. Originally commissioned in 1701 by Frederick I of Prussia, the Room was later perfected Tsarskoe Selo, the Russian imperial city. In 1941, German troops invaded the Soviet Union, looting everything in their wake and seizing the Amber Room. When the Allies began the bombing of Germany in August 1944, the Room was hidden. And despite the best efforts of treasure hunters and art collectors from around the world, it has never been seen again." <br />Now, two powerful men have set their best operatives loose in pursuit, and the hunt has begun once more. . . . <br />Life is good for Atlanta judge Rachel Cutler. She loves her job, loves her kids, and remains civil to her ex-husband, Paul. But everything changes when her father, a man who survived the horrors of World War II, dies under strange circumstances--and leaves behind clues to a secret he kept his entire life . . . a secret about something called the Amber Room. <br />Desperate to know the truth about her father's suspicious dealings, Rachel takes off for Germany, with Paul close behind. Shortly after arriving, they find themselves involved with a cast of shadowy characters who all claim to share their quest. But as they learn more about the history of the treasure they seek, Rachel and Paul realize they're in way over their heads. Locked in a treacherous game with ruthless professional killers and embroiled in a treasure hunt of epic proportions, Rachel and Paul suddenly find themselves on a collisioncourse with the forces of power, evil, and history itself. <br />A brilliant adventure and a scintillating tale of intrigue, deception, art, and murder, "The Amber Room" is a classic tale of suspense--and the debut of a strong new voice in the world of the international thriller. "From the Hardcover edition.</span>

<div id="review_21844953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21844953" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/985163-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1279729755p2/985163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21844953?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/985163-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780739354070" href="/book/show/913461.The_Amber_Room">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People that want to punish themselves</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=nazism">nazism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=art-history">art-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=russia">russia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=world-war-two">world-war-two</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=couldn-t-finish">couldn-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/985163-ann?shelf=1940s">1940s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21844953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11168256192099242057">Oh <i>Amber Room</i>, how did I hate thee? Let me count the ways...<br/><br/>- Every German says "und" (instead of "and") even as they're speaking English.<br/><br/>- Women say "Damn you" to the man they're about to sleep with.<br/><br/>-"Damn" used in every other sentence: "The trail was easy to follow. Too damn easy."<br/><br/>-How much needless, random sex do you need in a book?<br/><br/>-Every cliche possible is used - my favorite: The greedy American treasure hunter is named McCoy and calls women "little lady". ARE YOU KIDDING ME????<br/><br/>-Crazy long p</span>
  <span id="freeText11168256192099242057" style="display:none">Oh <i>Amber Room</i>, how did I hate thee? Let me count the ways...<br /><br />- Every German says "und" (instead of "and") even as they're speaking English.<br /><br />- Women say "Damn you" to the man they're about to sleep with.<br /><br />-"Damn" used in every other sentence: "The trail was easy to follow. Too damn easy."<br /><br />-How much needless, random sex do you need in a book?<br /><br />-Every cliche possible is used - my favorite: The greedy American treasure hunter is named McCoy and calls women "little lady". ARE YOU KIDDING ME????<br /><br />-Crazy long paragraphs of description of the history behind the Amber Room - any competent writer would have been able to put that information in the action without resorting to pages of exposition. Or even in shorter exposition!<br /><br />-The female protagonist is "feisty", and her Russian, widowed father lovingly says that "she's just like her mother". Oh wow, another cliche! For the record, the character wasn't feisty - she was just bitchy.<br /><br />-I listened to the audio-version of this, and the reader made every German sound exactly the same, and exactly like the gay German alias on the movie <i>The Saint</i>.<br /><br />Unbelievably bad. I got to the last disc of the 13 disc set and couldn't do anymore, even though I was so close to the end. Maybe it turned brilliant in that last disc?? I just didn't care. I wanted to like it because I thought the premise seemed so interesting, but it was horrible. Every character makes the stupidest decisions you can possibly imagine, and there is scarcely a character to even like, let alone care about. I suppose, to be fair, I should admit that I hate almost all thrillers, but there are intelligent thrillers of this type out there (<i>The Eight</i>, <i>The Book of Q</i>), so there's just no excuse for using such potentially good material and turning it into something so bad. It's officially in my list of the worst books I've ever read.<br /><br />To add to my annoyance, I realized after looking at some reviews on Amazon that the reader of the audiobook was also pronouncing the German names incorrectly. Ugh!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11168256192099242057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172525182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172525182" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4484023-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577929655p2/4484023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172525182?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/4484023-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who love awesome first chapters followed by 45 horrible ones</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bonnie by: </span>
      the prospect of a 5 hour busride without something to read
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4484023-bonnie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4484023-bonnie?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172525182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13001482550923720387">I have one word that sums up my feelings for this book, and unfortunately, 90% of <i>The Amber Room's</i> dialogue content: "Hardly." <br/><br/>Defined:<br/>1.Only just; almost not; barely: We had hardly reached the lake when it started raining. hardly any; hardly ever.<br/>2. not at all; scarcely: That report is hardly surprising.<br/>3. with little likelihood: He will hardly come now. <br/><br/>A few samples:<br/>"They didn't have forklifts?"<br/>"Hardly."<br/><br/>She motioned to the art. "A connoisseur?"<br/>"Hardly."<br/><br/>"I'm waiting," the female voice said.<br/>"An</span>
  <span id="freeText13001482550923720387" style="display:none">I have one word that sums up my feelings for this book, and unfortunately, 90% of <i>The Amber Room's</i> dialogue content: "Hardly." <br /><br />Defined:<br />1.Only just; almost not; barely: We had hardly reached the lake when it started raining. hardly any; hardly ever.<br />2. not at all; scarcely: That report is hardly surprising.<br />3. with little likelihood: He will hardly come now. <br /><br />A few samples:<br />"They didn't have forklifts?"<br />"Hardly."<br /><br />She motioned to the art. "A connoisseur?"<br />"Hardly."<br /><br />"I'm waiting," the female voice said.<br />"And patience is not one of your virtues?"<br />"Hardly."<br /><br />"Maybe it's genetic?"<br />"Hardly."<br /><br />Knoll obviously hadn't sensed her presence, thinking he'd rid himself of her in the Atlanta airport.<br />Not hardly, Christian.<br /><br />"That shaft is hardly big enough for three people to walk through."<br /><br />She gestured to the blossoms. "Garden?"<br />"Hardly."<br /><br />"Sounds like you're developing a heart, Christian."<br />... YOU GUESSED IT. "Hardly."<br /><br />GET ANOTHER ADVERB.<br /><br />This story had potential; it really did. When I grabbed it off the shelf in Penn Station, it was the Nazis, stolen art, war, Acquisitors, rich old men willing to kill people, and promising villains that intrigued me. But somewhere along the way I started realizing that while Amber is pretty and all, it was way cooler in Jurassic Park when it fossilized mosquitoes with dinosaur DNA. I was also tricked into reading it because the main characters were lawyers "doing some very unlawyerly things" as Mr. Berry himself explained in the cute little interview in the back. He likes to "break stereotypes," he says. Well, sometimes that sad old stereotype that mothers take care of their kids, and don't run off to certain death in Stod at a moment's notice over a hunk of rock, may just ring truer than breaking it.<br /><br />I like fun, globe-trotting adventure stories. I appreciate research. I did not like <i>The Da Vinci Code</i>. Dan Brown writes <i>The Amber Room</i> is "[m]y kind of thriller." <br /><br />Well folks, is this my kind of thriller?<br />... ________.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13001482550923720387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16915566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16915566" />
    <a title="Andy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31891-andy"><img alt="Andy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241280938p2/31891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16915566?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/31891-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16915566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7710366375163198781">A mediocre novel at best. If you're looking for a reasonably entertaining book for a long airplane ride then this might do the trick. Otherwise, I think there are much better books of this genre out there. While the concept of recovering lost art treasures that were looted by the Nazis in WWII is a fascinating one, and the historical info about the actual Amber Room is also quite interesting, the author just can't put it all together into a compelling story. One of the biggest problems is that t</span>
  <span id="freeText7710366375163198781" style="display:none">A mediocre novel at best. If you're looking for a reasonably entertaining book for a long airplane ride then this might do the trick. Otherwise, I think there are much better books of this genre out there. While the concept of recovering lost art treasures that were looted by the Nazis in WWII is a fascinating one, and the historical info about the actual Amber Room is also quite interesting, the author just can't put it all together into a compelling story. One of the biggest problems is that the protagonists just aren't likable, and it doesn't help that by far the most interesting character in the book (Karol Borya) is killed off very early. In fact, it's Borya's murder that is the catalyst for the entire storyline of the novel so it's not a "spoiler" mentioning this here. Overall I give the author credit for the concept and for making a valiant attempt at an exciting novel. I definitely liked the European locales, but the villains, know as "Acquisitors," who scour the world for rare and stolen art treasures for their wealthy employers, who act more like trained assassins was a bit much. I found myself skimming a lot of pages in the final third to get through this one . Not horrible, but just not that good either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7710366375163198781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2989427986?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C." href="/user/show/10501026-c">C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345483430" href="/book/show/661749.The_Amber_Room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10501026-c?shelf=riedel-titles-2019">riedel-titles-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2989427986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7872767014477356896">I bought “<b>The Amber Room</b>”, 2003, over ten years ago, scooping up bargains of modern releases. I rarely read men, even though some produce the most beautiful writing; like Farley Mowat and Cleveland Amory. Men’s books tend towards violence. This novel began with a Nazi torture prologue and contained a sexual assault attempt. The male thief was easy to hate and murdered nearly everyone. What I appreciated is a puzzle based on reality that spanned Germany, Czechoslovakia, and Russia. It is <b>Steve Be</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7872767014477356896" style="display:none">I bought “<b>The Amber Room</b>”, 2003, over ten years ago, scooping up bargains of modern releases. I rarely read men, even though some produce the most beautiful writing; like Farley Mowat and Cleveland Amory. Men’s books tend towards violence. This novel began with a Nazi torture prologue and contained a sexual assault attempt. The male thief was easy to hate and murdered nearly everyone. What I appreciated is a puzzle based on reality that spanned Germany, Czechoslovakia, and Russia. It is <b>Steve Berry’s</b> modus operandi to write historical intrigue and if I liked this novel, I have others.<br /><br />I enjoyed “<b>The Amber Room</b>” at a three-star level. To the good, Rachel is a judge. She and her ex-husband, Paul, take time to like but her war surviving, eighty-three year-old Father, Karol, is loveable. Rachel and Paul discover that Karol and Paul’s parents had ideas about where the famous Russian masterpiece was stashed in 1941, as does as his war surviving, loyal Czech friend. I saw reviews calling this novel poorly-written, which removed expectations so that I liked it adequately. It was always action-packed, not boring. What tamped down the thrill is that narrating a villain is a waste of pages for me. I want to stick with one protagonist or two and want only their perspectives. I waited out chapters of the murderous thief and a slightly more likeable woman thief.<br /><br />Secondly, <b>Steve</b> did provide a fictional conclusion about the Amber Room but it was not an exciting place; not a triumphant, clue-following, dramatic retrieval that adventure readers seek. I loved the twist of befriending an American tycoon, who is heroic and not the textbook irritant that he appears to be! The grace and heart of Rachel’s beloved Russian Father and his equally loveable old Czech friend came across nicely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7872767014477356896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6179849400004170566">I didn't much like DaVinci Code, but since I met Steve Berry and liked what he had to say about writing, I thought I'd give this one a try. I may now be in love with the genre. It combines what I love about historical fiction--history lessons--with another area of learning--learning about art--and Berry's novel is a much better, more satisfying read than Dan Brown's.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132405501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132405501" />
    <a title="Nick Brett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970422-nick-brett"><img alt="Nick Brett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266451680p2/2970422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132405501?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Brett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Brett" href="/user/show/2970422-nick-brett">Nick Brett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132405501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13035664562774503852">The Amber Room was a treasure looted by the Nazis and lost during the end of WW2. Worth an on-line search to understand the background, it's quite interesting.<br/>And Steve Berry's debut novel is a thriller based around the story. While there are similarities to the many types of book dealing with lost treasures, it was refreshing and interesting to have the WW2 elements and for it not to be the usual search for Jesus' sandal, Hercules lunch box or the lost MacDonald's of Atlantis. Yep, we do have a</span>
  <span id="freeText13035664562774503852" style="display:none">The Amber Room was a treasure looted by the Nazis and lost during the end of WW2. Worth an on-line search to understand the background, it's quite interesting.<br />And Steve Berry's debut novel is a thriller based around the story. While there are similarities to the many types of book dealing with lost treasures, it was refreshing and interesting to have the WW2 elements and for it not to be the usual search for Jesus' sandal, Hercules lunch box or the lost MacDonald's of Atlantis. Yep, we do have a couple involved (I think that must be in the unofficial rules) and ruthless killers, but this is actually well written and well researched. The "suddenly, as rare things will, it vanished" is a quote from Browning and is used during the book, it's an apt and appropriate quote.<br /><br /><br />US Judge follows the trail of the Amber Room once her father is killed and she discovers he was involved in the search for the room at the back end of the war. It appears he had a secret that he kept until his death. Judge's estranged husband joins her as they follow the trail through the types of adventures and close calls that we have now come to expect of these books.<br /><br />Well written and quite good fun if you like these kind of things.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13035664562774503852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2846318491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2846318491" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10978428-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601301778p2/10978428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2846318491?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/10978428-jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846318491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9035584110198907448"> Been reading World War II novels and, yep, here's another one. Actually, most of the story is set in postwar Europe. The story begins at the end of the war and involves one of WWII's biggest mysteries--what happened to the fabulous treasure of The Amber Room? This was a room with walls made of exquisite amber panels (and including jewels) of the Catherine Palace near St. Petersburg. After the Germans invaded the Soviet Union in 1941, they reached the palace (then a Soviet museum) and looted the</span>
  <span id="freeText9035584110198907448" style="display:none"> Been reading World War II novels and, yep, here's another one. Actually, most of the story is set in postwar Europe. The story begins at the end of the war and involves one of WWII's biggest mysteries--what happened to the fabulous treasure of The Amber Room? This was a room with walls made of exquisite amber panels (and including jewels) of the Catherine Palace near St. Petersburg. After the Germans invaded the Soviet Union in 1941, they reached the palace (then a Soviet museum) and looted the amazing treasure-- and took it to Germany. During the Allied bombing of Germany, it was hidden away--and never seen again. In Steve Berry's story, an American woman finds some clues to the whereabouts of the Amber Room--and begins a treasure hunt for it. But she's not the only one, as there are ruthless men also looking for it. So it's a fast-paced thriller with plenty of twists and turns. But what I think I like most about this book is that it is based on good research. In a short Writer's Note at the end, Berry separates fact from fiction and suggests what he thinks actually happened to The Amber Room.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_489278888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489278888" />
    <a title="Lance Charnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7296900-lance-charnes"><img alt="Lance Charnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442653554p2/7296900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489278888?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lance Charnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lance Charnes" href="/user/show/7296900-lance-charnes">Lance Charnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345504388" href="/book/show/2671179-the-amber-room">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who want a Dan Brown story without needing Cliff Notes to understand it</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7296900-lance-charnes?shelf=fiction-thrillers-adventure">fiction-thrillers-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7296900-lance-charnes?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489278888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14226168735696682566"><i>The Amber Room</i> is a much like the kind of tale I write – an international thriller with an everyman protagonist (in this case, an everyman and everywoman) who gets by with whatever native intelligence and wits he/she brings to the party. It was Steve Berry’s first published novel, one of three he wrote before he drifted into Dan Brown territory with his Cotton Malone series, and as such it still has some mooring in the real world.<br/><br/>The Amber Room is the near-legendary Czarist treasure stolen by th</span>
  <span id="freeText14226168735696682566" style="display:none"><i>The Amber Room</i> is a much like the kind of tale I write – an international thriller with an everyman protagonist (in this case, an everyman and everywoman) who gets by with whatever native intelligence and wits he/she brings to the party. It was Steve Berry’s first published novel, one of three he wrote before he drifted into Dan Brown territory with his Cotton Malone series, and as such it still has some mooring in the real world.<br /><br />The Amber Room is the near-legendary Czarist treasure stolen by the Nazis from the Soviet Union during WWII. The amber-encrusted wall panels disappeared at the end of the war, leaving behind a number of conflicting theories regarding their fate. This much is true. Where Berry comes in: two wealthy art collectors – who steal stolen artworks for their own uses – now compete with each other to find the now-priceless panels. Their henchpeople – one man, one woman, both of course beautiful, sexy, adept sociopaths – canvass the U.S. and Europe for clues to the room’s location.<br /><br />Enter our protagonists: Paul and Rachel Cutler, he a lawyer, she a judge. Rachel’s elderly father happens to be one of the few people alive who has a handle on the Amber Room’s final stop. When he ends up suddenly dead, Rachel decides to investigate, and Paul decides to follow to keep her out of trouble. That they run afoul of those two beautiful, sexy, adept, sociopathic henchpeople and become deeply enmeshed in the hunt for the Amber Room should come as no shock to you.<br /><br />The big surprise here isn’t in the plot – if you’ve read enough of these, you’ll have a pretty good idea where things are going before they get there – but in what good company the Cutlers are. They act and think like normal (albeit highly educated) people. Divorced but not hateful, they have lingering feelings for each other, and both are devoted to their children. At one time or another, one or the other is quite ready to stop and go home; I can’t recall Dan Brown’s Robert Langdon ever deciding to say “to hell with it” when the Forces of Darkness gather around him. The Cutlers make mistakes and trust the wrong people and learn from their missteps. And, like real people, they sometimes do things they haven’t thought through and for which they don’t have clear motives. In a genre in which both protagonists and villains always seem to know everything and know how to do everything, it’s enormously refreshing to tag along with characters who don’t make you feel hopelessly ignorant and incompetent.<br /><br />The henchpeople – Knoll (he) and Danzer (she) – are largely interchangeable, amoral in the usual ways, with roughly similar tastes and proclivities (why is it that in thrillers, the more evil you are, the more and better the sex that you have?). But at least they have reasons for being the way they are, and they’re merely sociopaths and not psychotics. Their masters are also largely interchangeable, wealthy beyond bounds and living in medieval Central European castles bedecked with their ill-gotten loot. The sameness of the antagonists is one of the key failings of this book. The historical downloads are usually motivated and usually end before they get irritating, although characters sometimes repeat themselves. The settings are well-drawn and easily visualized and will look swell in the inevitable Showtime or Starz original movie.<br /><br /><i>The Amber Room</i> is a fine way to spend a few hours if you’re into search-for-treasure thrillers. It’s like Dan Brown lite, without the attached reading list and with better writing. The protagonists prove that not every thriller hero has to be ex-Special Forces or World’s Foremost Expert in anything, and it’s a nice change to not have the fate of the known universe hanging in the balance. A good time was had by all.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14226168735696682566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43708917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041270544884193233">I chose the book because I have been following Steve Berry's Cotton Malone series, and I wanted to see what's going to be my reaction to his stand-alone novels. My two stars should not be misinterpreted. It was a well-researched book. My only complaint are the illogical actions of Judge Cutler and her ex-husband, Paul as they go following the clues behind the death of Rachel's father. During the war, Rachel's father was a POW in a Nazi camp, and he witnessed the interrogation and murder of sever</span>
  <span id="freeText17041270544884193233" style="display:none">I chose the book because I have been following Steve Berry's Cotton Malone series, and I wanted to see what's going to be my reaction to his stand-alone novels. My two stars should not be misinterpreted. It was a well-researched book. My only complaint are the illogical actions of Judge Cutler and her ex-husband, Paul as they go following the clues behind the death of Rachel's father. During the war, Rachel's father was a POW in a Nazi camp, and he witnessed the interrogation and murder of several soldiers who knew about the theft and possible location of the the Amber Room. <br />Being a judge, I would think that Rachel would have more respect for the law and police procedure. Instead, she and Paul (although they are already divorced, they are still in love with each other), go off to Europe and tries to follow the trail of clues. Assassination attempts by two treasure hunters who are also searching for the treasure is not going to stop them. Even after Rachel was sure that the guy who saved her from a car accident (it was staged) tried to kill her, she kept it a secret from the investigators and her ex-husband, because she found the guy attractive. Hey, if somebody ever tried to kill me, I don't care how hot she looks. I'm going to be telling everybody who wants to listen about the attempt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17041270544884193233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_141348061" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141348061" />
    <a title="Ithlilian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian"><img alt="Ithlilian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392859819p2/4793655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141348061?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ithlilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ithlilian" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian">Ithlilian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4793655-ithlilian?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141348061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7423582268106568475">Unfortunately, an interesting idea does not make a good novel. People who try to look for panels of amber that were once located in a Russian palace turn up dead. The main character's father may know more than he is telling his daughter, but he is murdered. So begins the hunt for the amber room with 2 crazy killers, some old men, and a divorced couple. That may sound a little cynical, but after sitting through this novel I'm a little annoyed.<br/><br/>The history behind the amber room is interesting. The </span>
  <span id="freeText7423582268106568475" style="display:none">Unfortunately, an interesting idea does not make a good novel. People who try to look for panels of amber that were once located in a Russian palace turn up dead. The main character's father may know more than he is telling his daughter, but he is murdered. So begins the hunt for the amber room with 2 crazy killers, some old men, and a divorced couple. That may sound a little cynical, but after sitting through this novel I'm a little annoyed.<br /><br />The history behind the amber room is interesting. The killers and what they do for a living is interesting. Uncovering little bits of information that leads the characters to a mountain is also interesting. Continuing the story once the location of the amber room was obvious is just painful. If you are paying attention you will know what happened to the amber room about half way into the novel. Don't pat yourself on the back because you have to sit through the other half of the novel yelling at the main characters to put their thinking caps on. Maybe if this was told from the perspective of the divorced couple only it would have been tolerable, it actually may have been good. Adding in the perspective of the two treasure hunters reveals too much. As a reader, I can't learn behind the scenes information from one character and then pretend I'm ignorant while I read another character's point of view. This story is way too simple for how long it was, and by 3/4 of the way I was ready for it to be over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7423582268106568475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14616384689732137803" style="display:none">Wow! Berry's 1st outing is about as good as his others...,<br /><br />Being that this was Steve Berry's first book and I read his books out of order, I was pleasantly surprised to find that this was as well-written as his more recent outings. I read Berry's other three books before reading this and the only fault that I can find in this book is that he has outdone himself with each subsequent release. Basically, because he has gotten so good at the thriller genre, he makes his older books seem a little less impressive; thankfully, this book was still excellent. It kept me on edge from start to finish. This book was just another example of his unique writing style that keeps the reader entertained and enthralled from cover to cover.<br /><br />I cannot wait for Berry's next book. I am now a life-long Steve Berry fan.<br /><br />An excellent read with unexpected plot twists, vivid descriptions and excellent character development. Just shy of a 5/5 I would rate this as a 4.5/5...</span>

<div id="review_2314885588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer4745696260333831748">At the beginning this book was a tad confusing. So many characters from different parts of the world. Once I understood the characters I couldn’t put this book down. Highly recommend to anyone that enjoys historical fiction. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E Wilson" href="/user/show/2773711-e-wilson">E Wilson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer128717489&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128717489" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13325679692916552876"> <br/> This book had such a promising subject for a mystery and the<br/>author obviously researched amber and the amber room's history well.<br/>Then he threw it away in a mediocre novel with a truly unlikable<br/>heroine and her semi-wimpy ex-husband. I think it would have been<br/>much much better if he had written about Rachel's Father and his<br/>partner's attempt to find the treasure.<br/> There are so many implausible events starting with Rachel's<br/>decision to flit off to Europe and and leave her two young children as well as</span>
  <span id="freeText13325679692916552876" style="display:none"> <br /> This book had such a promising subject for a mystery and the<br />author obviously researched amber and the amber room's history well.<br />Then he threw it away in a mediocre novel with a truly unlikable<br />heroine and her semi-wimpy ex-husband. I think it would have been<br />much much better if he had written about Rachel's Father and his<br />partner's attempt to find the treasure.<br /> There are so many implausible events starting with Rachel's<br />decision to flit off to Europe and and leave her two young children as well as a contentious race for her judges seat. Maybe with her<br />judgement she should lose the race anyway. What Mother flies to Europe and doesn't call to check on her children and let whoever is taking care<br />of them know how she can be reached? Then on the spur of the moment her husband,Paul, takes off after her.Then,why was Christian ready to<br />kill her in the cave, but after she witnesses a killing he<br />lets her and her husband go with just a warning. They continue<br />running around Europe after almost being killed without a thought<br />of the kids back home. There were just so many incidents when I<br />was thinking "this just would not happen".<br /> This all may seem petty, but to me these unrealistic details<br />spoil the story for me especially when the author did such a fine<br />job of researching the amber room and amber itself.<br /> I listened to this on an audio book and I really wanted to <br />listen to the interview with the author, but it was already a<br />week overdue and I had to turn in in.<br /> </span>

<div id="review_166253963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166253963" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5386578-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547189949p2/5386578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166253963?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/5386578-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166253963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18418397032011983408">This is the first Steve Berry book that I read. He writes historical thrillers that lead the reader all over the world. He bases his main idea for the book in fact, and then takes a few liberties with the facts to make it a more readable story. Then at the end, he tells the reader what is true and what was made up. In this story, there are two sets of art thieves out to find some of the most expensive and beautiful art treasures in the world. Many were looted in WWII. The biggest prize is The Am</span>
  <span id="freeText18418397032011983408" style="display:none">This is the first Steve Berry book that I read. He writes historical thrillers that lead the reader all over the world. He bases his main idea for the book in fact, and then takes a few liberties with the facts to make it a more readable story. Then at the end, he tells the reader what is true and what was made up. In this story, there are two sets of art thieves out to find some of the most expensive and beautiful art treasures in the world. Many were looted in WWII. The biggest prize is The Amber Room, a room made from Baltic amber and taken to St. Petersburg, Russia. After the war, nobody is sure what happened, although it was suspected that the amber was sold off bit by bit. In the book, the two main art thieves are playing cat and mouse with each other and trying to find this fabulous prize. Does someone have it hiding somewhere? You'll have to read the book to find out! The Amber Room has been since recreated, and you can see pictures of it on Flicker.com. It is indescrbably beautiful. I think you will enjoy Steve Berry's writing, since he has good, fast moving plotlines, and you can always learn a bit of history too!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18418397032011983408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126652681" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126652681" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3444927-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321249p2/3444927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126652681?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/3444927-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345504388" href="/book/show/2671179-the-amber-room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3444927-suzanne?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3444927-suzanne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126652681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4742648750247849391">Let me just say that this has to be the best Steve Berry novel that I have read to date! <br/><br/>Art historians everywhere would love to know what happened to the Amber Room after it disappeared during WWII. Berry paints a wonderful tale of what might have happened to it in a story that chronicles the adventures of Atlanta judge Rachel Cutler when she travels to Europe to get to the bottom of this mystery after her father Karol Borya, was killed because of what he knew about the Amber Room's whereabouts</span>
  <span id="freeText4742648750247849391" style="display:none">Let me just say that this has to be the best Steve Berry novel that I have read to date! <br /><br />Art historians everywhere would love to know what happened to the Amber Room after it disappeared during WWII. Berry paints a wonderful tale of what might have happened to it in a story that chronicles the adventures of Atlanta judge Rachel Cutler when she travels to Europe to get to the bottom of this mystery after her father Karol Borya, was killed because of what he knew about the Amber Room's whereabouts. Rachel gets mixed up in the race between two European industrialists/art collectors to find the Amber Room, and almost loses her life in the process. The big question is who will find it first, and does it actually exist? <br /><br />For art history buffs, this novel offers an entertaining and intriguing look at one of the art world's most famous mysteries. I was sitting on the edge of my seat through at least half the novel! If you like this novel, I also recommend Jeffrey Archer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4742648750247849391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145236135" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1372184-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219412802p2/1372184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145236135?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/1372184-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345504388" href="/book/show/2671179-the-amber-room">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145236135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11464383449352793387">I gave this book an extra star because of the research put in to it, but I really didn't like it. The father is the best-written character, for whom the reader feels most connection to, but he gets killed off right away. The next-best written characters? The bad guys. And not best-written bad guys. Nope, more interest is paid to them and their relationships than the protagonists, even when they're just killing people indiscriminately. They're written with far more sympathy than the actual protag</span>
  <span id="freeText11464383449352793387" style="display:none">I gave this book an extra star because of the research put in to it, but I really didn't like it. The father is the best-written character, for whom the reader feels most connection to, but he gets killed off right away. The next-best written characters? The bad guys. And not best-written bad guys. Nope, more interest is paid to them and their relationships than the protagonists, even when they're just killing people indiscriminately. They're written with far more sympathy than the actual protagonists, who, really, seem to make one bad relational decision after another (until the very end, when it all wraps up very neatly). I liked The Romanov Prophecy and the Cotton Malone series sounds interesting, but I'm glad I didn't recommend this for my book club.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11464383449352793387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was also fascinating that last Tuesday there was an article in the newspaper about</span>

<div id="review_1495920134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1495920134" />
    <a title="Matt Halpern" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46759159-matt-halpern"><img alt="Matt Halpern" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533205763p2/46759159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1495920134?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt Halpern" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt Halpern" href="/user/show/46759159-matt-halpern">Matt Halpern</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345504388" href="/book/show/2671179-the-amber-room">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1495920134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16248721316385980458">Steve Berry's writing style is very reminiscent of Dan Brown. The difference that I have found with this book though is that Berry's approach is not about the symbols like Brown, but about the story as a whole. I really enjoyed this book and am looking forward to reading more of his work.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1281746310?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cold War Conversations Podcast" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cold War Conversations Podcast" href="/user/show/5231504-cold-war-conversations-podcast">Cold War Conversations Podcast</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9781848943056" href="/book/show/19099626-the-amber-room">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1281746310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17834599122641002687"><b>Not brilliant, but a reasonably entertaining read</b><br/><br/>The premise is strong - "Acquisitors," who scour the world for rare and stolen art treasures for their wealthy employers, however the delivery is predictable and the characters are not too strong either.<br/><br/>The historical background of the Amber Room is quite interesting, but the story could have been so much better.<br/><br/>A decent holiday read, but not very memorable.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093289945" />
    <a title="Stephanie Jenkins Ortiz Cerrillo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34470690-stephanie-jenkins-ortiz-cerrillo"><img alt="Stephanie Jenkins Ortiz Cerrillo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409439902p2/34470690.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093289945?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Jenkins Ortiz Cerrillo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Jenkins Ortiz Cerrillo" href="/user/show/34470690-stephanie-jenkins-ortiz-cerrillo">Stephanie Jenkins Ortiz Cerrillo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093289945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14106908345696919227">A great book to read if your interested in the history based on WWII, German, Historical Treasures or the Soviet Union. This book is based on the Search for the original Amber Room that spanned for more than 50 years. Can you imagine an entire room made from amber, sculptures, wall art, frames, furniture all sculpted by Amber and wood. I've often thought of all the lost and destroyed treasures from WWII and can only begin to imagine the magnificent pieces lost and the lives lost over such treasu</span>
  <span id="freeText14106908345696919227" style="display:none">A great book to read if your interested in the history based on WWII, German, Historical Treasures or the Soviet Union. This book is based on the Search for the original Amber Room that spanned for more than 50 years. Can you imagine an entire room made from amber, sculptures, wall art, frames, furniture all sculpted by Amber and wood. I've often thought of all the lost and destroyed treasures from WWII and can only begin to imagine the magnificent pieces lost and the lives lost over such treasures. This is a great take of suspense, a great adventure, a treasure hunt of epic proportion. I have to admit that I listen to this book on audio in very broken portions and I believe I would have given it a higher rating if I had read it or at least been able to listen to it in a more timely manor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14106908345696919227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I1NHqvYgWIbaLlOndRU6YH+KagKZyH69xCG9auUHr1P0HHc7nkD82bPR0LIx8dHVcAwSxYwI8EXl7L47e5MaKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('keagCmMoG6RN//4eJXyY8RlWNFET8dN5QRh7CwVTgghGqZCbC0i/+yQAfQthmHNEFtBMlgYxXYFg1Xham8c3cw==')})
  }

  <strong>
    <em>The Amber Room</em>
  </strong>
</a>. His books have been translated into 40 languages with 25,000,000 copies in 51 countries. They consistently appear in the top echelon of <em>The New York Times,</em> <em>USA Today,</em> and Indie bestseller lists.<br /><br />History lies at the heart of every Steve Berry novel. It’s his passion, one he shares with his wife, Elizabeth, which led them to create History Matters, a foundation dedicated to historic preservation. Since 2009 Steve and Elizabeth have crossed the country to save endangered historic treasures, raising money via lectures, receptions, galas, luncheons, dinners and their popular writers’ workshops. To date, 3,500 students have attended those workshops with over $1.5 million dollars raised.<br /><br />Steve’s devotion to historic preservation was recognized by the American Library Association, which named Steve its spokesperson for National Preservation Week. Among his other honors are the Royden B. Davis Distinguished Author Award; the Barnes &amp; Noble Writers for Writers Award given by Poets &amp; Writers; the Anne Frank Human Writes Award; and the Silver Bullet, bestowed by International Thriller Writers for his philanthropic work. He has been chosen both the Florida and Georgia Writer of the Year. He's also an emeritus member of the Smithsonian Libraries Advisory Board. In 2010, a NPR survey named <strong>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/books/the-templar-legacy/synopsis/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <em>The Templar Legacy</em>
  </a>
</strong> one of the top 100 thrillers ever written.<br /><br />Steve was born and raised in Georgia, graduating from the Walter F. George School of Law at Mercer University. He was a trial lawyer for 30 years and held elective office for 14 of those years. He is a founding member of International Thriller Writers—a group of nearly 6,000 thriller writers from around the world—and served three years as its co-president.<br /><br /><a title="FAQ" href="https://www.goodreads.com/faq/" rel="nofollow noopener">CLICK</a> for more detailed bio information in FAQ.<br /><br /><a title="History Matters" href="http://history-matters.org/" target="_b" rel="nofollow noopener"></a></span>
